<div id="review_1769045840" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1769045840" />
    <a title="Kitty" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9823700-kitty"><img alt="Kitty" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506670454p2/9823700.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1769045840?book_show_action=true">Sep 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kitty" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kitty" href="/user/show/9823700-kitty">Kitty</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9823700-kitty?shelf=love-to-hate">love-to-hate</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1769045840&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1769045840" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8594298872310316728">This is one of the most horrifying books I've ever read. Even more horrifying are all the 5 star reviews on it and women saying that it saved their marriage or changed their life.<br/><br/>This is a story of a woman being emotionally abused by her husband, and God (and His noble messengers) telling her to suck it up and stop being such a whiny fucking bitch. That's it. That's the book. She gets back with a man who makes major life decisions for their family without consulting her, blames her for everythin</span>
  <span id="freeText8594298872310316728" style="display:none">This is one of the most horrifying books I've ever read. Even more horrifying are all the 5 star reviews on it and women saying that it saved their marriage or changed their life.<br /><br />This is a story of a woman being emotionally abused by her husband, and God (and His noble messengers) telling her to suck it up and stop being such a whiny fucking bitch. That's it. That's the book. She gets back with a man who makes major life decisions for their family without consulting her, blames her for everything, verbally abuses her (saying every horrible thing and misogynistic slur he can think of), disparages her parenting, her decorating, her social life, every little choice she makes. She is hurt and confused by his coldness, the way his work (and even his brand new car) are way more of a priority than her or her children, his abandonment of her while her mother is dying, and his infidelity, but things get cleared up with a woman who treated her like an idiot for not being bourgeoisie calls her up and tells her she's a spoiled brat for not being happy for the man who is mistreating her and her children. There's more but why would I go on? This should be enough.<br /><br />Yikes, Francine. Are you okay? How is your marriage? Why are you so obsessed with heterosexual age gap relationships working out? Why couldn't she have married the millionaire who treated her like a goddess? What is the matter with you? Do you realize what you're modeling for women? You need to read Right Wing Woman by Andrea Dworkin. You drive me fucking crazy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8594298872310316728" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/222010850" />
    <a title="Danielle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5227213-danielle"><img alt="Danielle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1302026840p2/5227213.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/222010850?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Danielle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Danielle" href="/user/show/5227213-danielle">Danielle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5227213-danielle?shelf=christian-fiction">christian-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer222010850" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16789297203599646600">This book certainly was not what I was expecting. It tells the story of Sierra Madrid (a name I found painful to constantly read), a woman who has it all until her husband decides to take a new job in a city far from their hometown. This event begins a journey down a long road of hurt, betrayal, and redemption. While reading about Sierra's life, we also read along with her as she goes through the diary of an ancestor whose circumstances mirror Sierra's in many ways.<br/><br/>This book was painful for me t</span>
  <span id="freeText16789297203599646600" style="display:none">This book certainly was not what I was expecting. It tells the story of Sierra Madrid (a name I found painful to constantly read), a woman who has it all until her husband decides to take a new job in a city far from their hometown. This event begins a journey down a long road of hurt, betrayal, and redemption. While reading about Sierra's life, we also read along with her as she goes through the diary of an ancestor whose circumstances mirror Sierra's in many ways.<br /><br />This book was painful for me to read because I have gone through a divorce. If anything, Francine Rivers is the queen of realistically barabed conversations between people in relationship. You can feel the wounds the words inflict, and that is hard to go through as a reader. The first book I noticed this "talent" in was Her Mother's Hope, and at least in that book the pain was worth it in a good story. In this book, the redemption doesn't bring nearly enough soothing to those wounds that the reader has taken, in some degree, with Sierra. I wouldn't say Sierra was worth it as a character to go through that experience with her, if that makes sense.<br /><br />In other books by this author I have felt an element of spiritual growth, but I cannot say that for this book. This is not one that I'd recommend for another reader.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16789297203599646600" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a title="Megan Miller" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Megan Miller" href="/user/show/36209961-megan-miller">Megan Miller</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer15698844130845758876">So I started this book way back in like May or something, on the Kindle app, and totally forgot it existed until a couple days ago. But I busted my way through almost half of it in two days, so it wasn't a hard read or anything. haha<br/>Anyway.<br/>This was a really good book. Not my new favorite, but good. Well-written, honest characters. It's strongly in the genre of Christian Fiction For Women. (Not Amish or Historical Christian Fiction though, which is a different thing entirely.) Those have been ste</span>
  <span id="freeText15698844130845758876" style="display:none">So I started this book way back in like May or something, on the Kindle app, and totally forgot it existed until a couple days ago. But I busted my way through almost half of it in two days, so it wasn't a hard read or anything. haha<br />Anyway.<br />This was a really good book. Not my new favorite, but good. Well-written, honest characters. It's strongly in the genre of Christian Fiction For Women. (Not Amish or Historical Christian Fiction though, which is a different thing entirely.) Those have been steadily climbing down my list of Books I Enjoy, so I have a few bones to pick with it. But nothing I feel like writing about here.<br />Unrelated, it felt like the arc was maybe awkward. Like, the climax for me was kind of way before the actual intended climax and then what I think was the intended climax was vaguely anticlimactic. (Kind of like the structure of that sentence.) I'm not well-versed in Technical Writing Terminology, though, so what do I know.<br />Maybe closer to three stars just for personal enjoyment, but I do really, really love the heart of this book. So four it is. Here's to the scarlet thread in all our lives, and Jesus taking all our messes and turning them into beauty.</span>

<div id="review_136629862" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/136629862" />
    <a title="Lynai" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1470974-lynai"><img alt="Lynai" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386837151p2/1470974.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/136629862?book_show_action=true">Dec 26, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lynai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lynai" href="/user/show/1470974-lynai">Lynai</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1470974-lynai?shelf=own-a-copy">own-a-copy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer136629862" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15239773378015995072"><i>The Scarlet Thread</i> is a story about two women separated by time but sharing the same experiences and learning the same lessons together. Sierra is the modern woman who is battling marital problems while Mary Catherine McMurray is Sierra’s ancestor who was forced to make a journey on the Oregon trail. The story about Mary Catherine was set in the 1800s and was told through her journal, the entries of which I had a hard time reading at first especially during the parts where Mary Catherine did not</span>
  <span id="freeText15239773378015995072" style="display:none"><i>The Scarlet Thread</i> is a story about two women separated by time but sharing the same experiences and learning the same lessons together. Sierra is the modern woman who is battling marital problems while Mary Catherine McMurray is Sierra’s ancestor who was forced to make a journey on the Oregon trail. The story about Mary Catherine was set in the 1800s and was told through her journal, the entries of which I had a hard time reading at first especially during the parts where Mary Catherine did not yet know how to write or spell. But as her writing progressed, her spelling also improved as well as her character and relationship to God. By reading Mary Catherine’s journal, Sierra was able to find answers to her problems as well as find comfort that her struggles are the same with her ancestor.<br /><br />I love that <i>The Scarlet Thread</i> is a tale that centers on issues about marriage, of the little things that seem harmless at first but would eventually contribute to its destruction such as unresolved conflicts and miscommunication. I learned a lot from this book especially on how to handle marital problems as well as family issues. There are just a few things that I find loose such as the friendship between Sierra and Marcia. I feel that a few emphasis should have been given to their friendship and more development on Marcia’s character. Nonetheless, the story is still great and can create an impact to every receptive reader.<br /><br /><i>The Scarlet Thread</i> is a book that every Christian will greatly appreciate. It tells about how when we start to mend our relationship with God, our relationships with other people will start to be okay as well. We cannot mend broken relationships on our own because as humans we are always imperfect but when we keep right with God, we eventually develop the character which our fellow men will find different in a restorative way. Now, I do not want to sound preachy here but these are the lessons I picked up while reading this book. I must say though that the redemption/conversion story of Sierra was a bit hurried compared to that of Mary Catherine. But then again, there have been conversion stories in real life that are as swift as Sierra’s. Who can question the work of God, anyway?<br /><br />All said, Francine Rivers remains to be one of my favorite authors and this is one book I highly recommend to everyone, including non-Christians who want to know more about the Christian God.<br /><br />Continue reading in <a href="http://lynaireads.luigiandlynai.net/2011/07/the-scarlet-threadfrancine-rivers/" rel="nofollow noopener"><strong>It's A Wonderful Bookworld</strong>.<br /><br /></a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15239773378015995072" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/79597605-april-reader?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/79597605-april-reader?shelf=troubled-marriage">troubled-marriage</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/79597605-april-reader?shelf=cheating-hero">cheating-hero</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2497208233" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6415446487951259359">Troubled marriage romances are like catnip for me because of the inherent angst that they come with. I enjoyed this book quite a bit but this was one situation when I wished that the heroine would leave the hero and find love elsewhere (Ron!). <br/><br/>Even though I’m a Christian, I’m not a fan of Christian romances. They’re too preachy for me and this one had moments that were off putting because of that (nothing wrong for people to enjoy it, just not my thing). <br/><br/>That said, it was well written and engagi</span>
  <span id="freeText6415446487951259359" style="display:none">Troubled marriage romances are like catnip for me because of the inherent angst that they come with. I enjoyed this book quite a bit but this was one situation when I wished that the heroine would leave the hero and find love elsewhere (Ron!). <br /><br />Even though I’m a Christian, I’m not a fan of Christian romances. They’re too preachy for me and this one had moments that were off putting because of that (nothing wrong for people to enjoy it, just not my thing). <br /><br />That said, it was well written and engaging for the most part. I just wish that either the hero took his head out of his butt a lot sooner and did some major grovelling or the heroine left him. I mean, he didn’t just cheat or have an affair. He left his wife for OW and made her feel like she’s less than dirt. He only started to realize that OW isn’t so great when her family treated him like crap at thanksgiving and then not long after that, OW was awful to his son. If not for those two instances, I’m not convinced that the hero would have left her so going back to the heroine ended up feeling like his second choice.<br /><br />I also wanted to add that I genuinely enjoyed the heroine’s personal journey (even though it was centred around her spirituality). Until her husband leaves her, she is completely dependent on him and is self-loathing and miserable when he starts acting like a jackass. She starts off as weak and petulant but slowly grows to learn her own self worth and strength. She has many opportunities to throw stuff in the hero’s face but she often shows restraint and maturity. Yes, telling him off more would have been nice but at the same time, it showed that she has control over her own emotions. <br /><br />I just wish that she ended up with nice guy Ron who had a thing for her. He appreciated her and was her best friend when she needed someone to talk to. I think I could have warmed a bit more towards the cheating husband if he repented much earlier in the book (it happens at the very end) and we’d see over time that he was slowly earning her trust back. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6415446487951259359" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_5216317" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/5216317" />
    <a title="Margaret Chind" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/226769-margaret-chind"><img alt="Margaret Chind" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470101584p2/226769.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/5216317?book_show_action=true">Aug 28, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Margaret Chind" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Margaret Chind" href="/user/show/226769-margaret-chind">Margaret Chind</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781414370637" href="/book/show/14331024-the-scarlet-thread">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/226769-margaret-chind?shelf=tyndale-house">tyndale-house</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/226769-margaret-chind?shelf=christianfiction">christianfiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/226769-margaret-chind?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/226769-margaret-chind?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer5216317" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11743316699405983847"><br/><a href='http://creativemadnessmama.com/blog/2012/06/09/the-scarlet-thread-by-francine-rivers/' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Originally posted on Creative Madness Mama</a> Originally published in 1996, now refreshed with a gorgeous new cover for 2012! <br/><blockquote>Read from June 08 to 09, 2012 — I own a copy</blockquote><br/>Reading the slight description blurb for this book does not even begin to touch on what all is inside. This Creative Madness Mama had the God-timing to accidentally pick this book up after a very frustrating disagreement with the Enginerd. This edition is a reprint with a gorgeous new cover (also just reprinted <a title='The Atonement Child by Francine Rivers' href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/14331040.The_Atonement_Child' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Atonement Child</a>)</span>
  <span id="freeText11743316699405983847" style="display:none"><br><a href="http://creativemadnessmama.com/blog/2012/06/09/the-scarlet-thread-by-francine-rivers/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Originally posted on Creative Madness Mama</a> Originally published in 1996, now refreshed with a gorgeous new cover for 2012! <br><blockquote>Read from June 08 to 09, 2012 — I own a copy</blockquote><br>Reading the slight description blurb for this book does not even begin to touch on what all is inside. This Creative Madness Mama had the God-timing to accidentally pick this book up after a very frustrating disagreement with the Enginerd. This edition is a reprint with a gorgeous new cover (also just reprinted <a title="The Atonement Child by Francine Rivers" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/14331040.The_Atonement_Child" rel="nofollow noopener">The Atonement Child</a>). As a person that loves matching book spines, seeing these new ones makes me really happy. Now back to the book... Asking now memory does not even begin to recall what the argument was about, but fury would best describe emotions present. This book and it's story is a God-send.<br><br>Characters through out this book are found in two different settings, one is contemporary (although written for 1996, everything still works well and fits as if it were 2012) and the other is historical in the time of Oregon Trail and heading west. With a combination of view points from sidelines to inside emotions and even a journal readers are kept captive from page one. This reader was not even planning to read this one yet as it just arrived and is not quite scheduled, but upon picking it up it became an impossibility to put it down until the wee hours of the morning and sleep demanded it. Even at around five hundred pages, this was read pretty quickly.<br><br>Into the heart, into the mind and soul this is a great read. I recommend it for anyone married or planning to get married. That's what this is about overall, marriage. Marriage between the love of your life and in the end the inclusion of God within that triune marriage. It's about a new marriage, an older marriage, a broken marriage, a fixed marriage and many things that influence a marriage in between. Filled with scripture and a friend, but not what some call overly preachy this book appeals.<br><p>
  <a href="http://www.francinerivers.com/books" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1441859454i/16160806._SX540_.jpg" alt="" width="750" height="150" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
  <br>
  <br>
</p> Other Reviews: <br> Marta's Legacy Saga: <br>

  <a href="http://creativemadnessmama.com/blog/2010/11/26/her-daughters-dream-by-fracine-rivers/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Her Daughter's Dream</a>

  <a href="http://wp.me/pYHD5-3OT" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

<div id="review_638679093" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/638679093" />
    <a title="Elizabeth Ray" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11564097-elizabeth-ray"><img alt="Elizabeth Ray" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1406844368p2/11564097.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/638679093?book_show_action=true">Jun 11, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elizabeth Ray" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elizabeth Ray" href="/user/show/11564097-elizabeth-ray">Elizabeth Ray</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer638679093&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer638679093" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11308578577375829282">I have mixed feelings about this book... On one hand, I did enjoy reading it and was very motivated to keep reading and finish it. On the other hand, I'm not sure how I feel about the message of the book- I feel like the woman was blamed way more than she should've been. Spoiler alert: There is NO excuse for having an affair; I don't care what your wife is like. Honestly, she had a legitimate reason to be ticked about having to move without having been consulted first. Yes, in Christian marriage</span>
  <span id="freeText11308578577375829282" style="display:none">I have mixed feelings about this book... On one hand, I did enjoy reading it and was very motivated to keep reading and finish it. On the other hand, I'm not sure how I feel about the message of the book- I feel like the woman was blamed way more than she should've been. Spoiler alert: There is NO excuse for having an affair; I don't care what your wife is like. Honestly, she had a legitimate reason to be ticked about having to move without having been consulted first. Yes, in Christian marriage, the man is the head of the household, but he is still supposed to consult his wife before major decisions and get her input and advice. Maybe if after the move he had remained a loving and kind husband and father, then I could agree with the author that the woman needed to change her behavior. However, he then continued to put his family on the back burner and success on the front. I can agree with the author that the wife was somewhat "at fault" and acted selfishly. In that way, it was a good lesson. However, I felt the man should've made more changes and more effort before he was worthy of being with again. Love is supposed to be unconditional, BUT even the Bible says divorce is allowed if one spouse is unfaithful. <br /><br />Oh, I forgot about the worst scene in the book! When the husband's mistress SLAPS the son and calls him racial slurs. The wife tries to hard not to lose her temper. Are you kidding me??? I would've been calling my lawyer or CPS! That's called righteous anger, woman!<br /><br />As for the second story, I was never able to get into it as much as the modern day story and was tempted to skip it to get to Sierra's story. I also thought her conversion was way too quick and easy. You don't go from hating and blaming God your whole life to being a dedicated follower in one instant. <br /><br />Overall, I did enjoy reading this book, but felt uncomfortable with some of the messages the author seemed to portray.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11308578577375829282" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_348440211" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/348440211" />
    <a title="Melissa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4818237-melissa"><img alt="Melissa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1335962346p2/4818237.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/348440211?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa" href="/user/show/4818237-melissa">Melissa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer348440211" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13007380291762074247">Francine Rivers is becoming one of my favorite authors. I just read The Scarlet Thread and what can I say but I loved it! This story is about two women in different times and the struggles that they go through. The characters we meet are Sierra Clanton Madrid and Mary Kathryn McMurray. These two women are related to each other but live years apart. Mary Kathryn’s is a pioneer woman struggling on the Oregon Trail and Sierra is a modern day wife that was also moved from her northern California hom</span>
  <span id="freeText13007380291762074247" style="display:none">Francine Rivers is becoming one of my favorite authors. I just read The Scarlet Thread and what can I say but I loved it! This story is about two women in different times and the struggles that they go through. The characters we meet are Sierra Clanton Madrid and Mary Kathryn McMurray. These two women are related to each other but live years apart. Mary Kathryn’s is a pioneer woman struggling on the Oregon Trail and Sierra is a modern day wife that was also moved from her northern California home to LA. This book deals with some heavy stuff. They find troubles in marriage, anger and not trusting God. Sierra finds her many greats ago grandma’s journal and reads. It is through the journal that Mary Kathryn helps Sierra’s with her struggles and Sierra finds what is old is new or rather is there ever any new? This book made me cry. It also reminded me that God’s love is patient and never ending and needs to be the center of your life. I did not want to put this book down. I can’t wait to find more of Francine Rivers’s books. I think it may be a Francine Rivers summer for me she is that good. I give this book a four star rating. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13007380291762074247" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('zM9fjKY0mmmaPRumASwHLEEDbAP5YoLoStcCn2zdBIulvybbrXPDASckoh/OF7Zrqq3tfPuallYsjrwIxyUdLA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('WuXqO7suUXSMgyLm9IyM7At4QlH2x5wIqBlsfU/0OqgzlZNssGkIHDGam187tz2r4NbDLvQ/iLbOQNLq5AwjDw==')})
  }
//]]>

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/6492.Francine_Rivers">About Francine Rivers</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer16426380954420019978">New York Times bestselling author Francine Rivers continues to win both industry acclaim and reader loyalty around the globe. Her numerous bestsellers include Redeeming Love, A Voice in the Wind, and Bridge to Haven, and her work has been translated into more than thirty different languages. She is a member of Romance Writers of America's coveted Hall of Fame as well as a recipient of the Lifetime</span>
  <span id="freeText16426380954420019978" style="display:none">New York Times bestselling author Francine Rivers continues to win both industry acclaim and reader loyalty around the globe. Her numerous bestsellers include Redeeming Love, A Voice in the Wind, and Bridge to Haven, and her work has been translated into more than thirty different languages. She is a member of Romance Writers of America's coveted Hall of Fame as well as a recipient of the Lifetime Achievement Award from American Christian Fiction Writers (ACFW). <br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.francinerivers.com">www.francinerivers.com</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.facebook.com/FrancineRivers">www.facebook.com/FrancineRivers</a> <br />Twitter: @FrancineRivers<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16426380954420019978" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
